Here is my summary of the concerns and opposition from the public about the new PNR directive:  - European Digital Rights (EDRI) campaign group:   - Five-year data retention period is too long.   - Directive may not prevent discriminatory profiling of individuals.   - Ineffective tool against terrorism.   - PNR was irrelevant in the Paris and Brussels bombings, as the attackers did not fly to Europe to carry out their attacks.  - EU Agency for Fundamental Rights (FRA):   - Effectiveness of PNR collection for crime prevention is questionable.   - Any such law needs to be backed up by statistical analysis to detect discrimination and measure the importance of PNR in crime investigations.  - Critics:   - EU should focus on improving intelligence-sharing between police forces.   - PNR data includes sensitive information such as race, religion, and sexual life, which should be protected to avoid infringing EU anti-discrimination law.   - No automatic data transfer from PIUs to comply with EU data protection legislation.  - Privacy concerns:   - European Court of Justice (ECJ) struck down an EU data retention directive in 2014, citing violations of fundamental privacy rights. Here is my summary of the concerns and opposition from the public about the new PNR directive:  - European Digital Rights (EDRI) campaign group:   - Five-year data retention period is too long.   - Directive may not prevent discriminatory profiling of individuals.   - Ineffective tool against terrorism, as PNR was irrelevant in the Paris and Brussels bombings. - EU Agency for Fundamental Rights (FRA):   - Effectiveness of PNR collection for crime prevention is questionable.   - Any such law needs to be backed up by statistical analysis to detect discrimination and measure the importance of PNR in crime investigations. - Critics:   - EU should focus on improving intelligence-sharing between police forces. - Privacy concerns:   - European Court of Justice (ECJ) struck down an EU data retention directive in 2014, citing violations of fundamental privacy rights.   - PNR data includes sensitive information such as race, religion, and sexual life, which must be deleted by PIUs to avoid infringing EU anti-discrimination law.   - No automatic data transfer from PIUs to comply with EU data protection legislation. **My Answer:** The number of UK fire and rescue staff taking long-term sick leave due to mental illness has increased by nearly a third over the last six years. In London, the figure has doubled since 2011-12, with 103 London fire staff taking mental health leave this year, some after working at Grenfell Tower. Two-thirds of fire services provided data, showing that the number of firefighters and other staff taking long-term mental health leave rose from 600 to 780 over the last six years. At least 126 staff have left the service due to mental health issues since 2011. In 2016-17, 97 Scottish fire staff and 111 Northern Irish fire staff took long-term mental health sick leave. A survey of over 1,600 staff and volunteers across emergency services found that nearly nine in 10 have experienced stress, low mood, or poor mental health, and one in four have considered suicide.  **Evaluation:**  **Answer (a):** - **Accuracy:** The statistics provided are accurate and directly reflect the information in the article. - **Helpfulness:** The answer is helpful as it includes all the key statistics mentioned in the article. - **Relevance:** The response is relevant, focusing on the statistics related to mental health issues among fire and rescue staff. - **Conciseness:** The answer is concise and does not include unnecessary information. - **Creativity and Novelty:** Not applicable for this type of summary. - **Missing Information:** The answer includes all the key statistics and does not miss any important information.  **Answer (b):** - **Accuracy:** The statistics provided are accurate and directly reflect the information in the article. - **Helpfulness:** The answer is helpful as it includes all the key statistics mentioned in the article. - **Relevance:** The response is relevant, focusing on the statistics related to mental health issues among fire and rescue staff. - **Conciseness:** The answer is concise and does not include unnecessary information. - **Creativity and Novelty:** Not applicable for this type of summary. - **Missing Information:** The answer includes all the key statistics and does not miss any important information. These metals include gold, copper, manganese, cobalt, and others. An assessment of the eastern Pacific, specifically the Clarion-Clipperton Zone, suggests that there are more than 27 billion tonnes of nodules, which contain significant quantities of these metals: seven billion tonnes of manganese, 340 million tonnes of nickel, 290 million tonnes of copper, and 78 million tonnes of cobalt. The United Nations, through the International Seabed Authority (ISA), has published a plan to manage the extraction of these minerals, and companies could start applying for licenses as early as 2016. They correctly identify the types and quantities of metals that can be extracted from the ocean floor. - **Conciseness:** Both answers are concise and to the point, without unnecessary information. - **Helpfulness:** Both answers are helpful in summarizing the potential benefits of deep sea mining. However, Answer (a) provides a bit more context by mentioning the role of the ISA in sharing the proceeds with developing countries, which adds a layer of information about the broader implications of deep sea mining. - **Creativity and Novelty:** Neither answer stands out in terms of creativity or novelty, as they both stick closely to the information provided in the article.  **Missing Information:** - Both answers could benefit from mentioning the potential environmental concerns and the debate among marine scientists, which are important aspects of the article.
